<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller">Rankings include all <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">provinces and territories</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Ontario</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">ɛər</span><span title="/iː/ or /ɪ/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-ca-Ontario.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/En-ca-Ontario.ogg" title="En-ca-Ontario.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ɔ̃taʁjo]</a></span>), one of the 13 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">provinces and territories of Canada</a>, is located in east-central <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QLocation_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-QLocation-8">[8]</a></sup> It is Canada's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_population" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by population">most populous province</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popont_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-popont-9">[9]</a></sup> accounting for nearly 40 percent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> of the country's population, and is the second-largest province in total area. Ontario is <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_area" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by area">fourth-largest in total area</a> when the territories of the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a> are included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-areaont_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-areaont-1">[1]</a></sup> It is home to the nation's capital city, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, and the nation's <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_100_largest_municipalities_in_Canada_by_population" title="List of the 100 largest municipalities in Canada by population">most populous</a> city, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ontario is bordered by the province of <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> to the east and northeast, and to the south by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> of (from west to east) <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>. Almost all of Ontario's 2,700 km (1,678 mi) border with the United States follows <a href="/wiki/Navigability" title="Navigability">inland waterways</a>: from the west at <a href="/wiki/Lake_of_the_Woods" title="Lake of the Woods">Lake of the Woods</a>, eastward along the major rivers and lakes of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>/<a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a> drainage system. These are the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_River_(Minnesota%E2%80%93Ontario)" title="Rainy River (Minnesota–Ontario)">Rainy River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_River_(Minnesota%E2%80%93Ontario)" title="Pigeon River (Minnesota–Ontario)">Pigeon River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">Lake Superior</a>, the <a href="/wiki/St._Marys_River_(Michigan%E2%80%93Ontario)" title="St. Marys River (Michigan–Ontario)">St. Marys River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">Lake Huron</a>, the <a href="/wiki/St._Clair_River" title="St. Clair River">St. Clair River</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Saint_Clair_(North_America)" title="Lake Saint Clair (North America)">Lake St. Clair</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">Detroit River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">Niagara River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a> and along the St. Lawrence River from <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston, Ontario</a>, to the Quebec boundary just east of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall,_Ontario" title="Cornwall, Ontario">Cornwall, Ontario</a>. There is only about 1 km (0.6 mi) of land border made up of portages including <a href="/wiki/Height_of_Land_Portage" title="Height of Land Portage">Height of Land Portage</a> on the Minnesota border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBC_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBC-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ontario is sometimes conceptually divided into two regions, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ontario" title="Northern Ontario">Northern Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a>. The great majority of Ontario's population and <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> is located in the south. In contrast, the larger, northern part of Ontario is sparsely populated with cold winters and heavy forestation.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The province is named after <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>, a term thought to be derived from <i>Ontarí:io</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_language" title="Wyandot language">Huron</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">Wyandot</a>) word meaning "great lake",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> or possibly <i>skanadario</i>, which means "beautiful water" in the <a href="/wiki/Iroquoian_languages" title="Iroquoian languages">Iroquoian languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Ontario has about 250,000 freshwater lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-river-number_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-river-number-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ontario" title="Geography of Ontario">Geography of Ontario</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Census_divisions_of_Ontario" title="Census divisions of Ontario">Census divisions of Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Canada" title="Geography of Canada">Geography of Canada</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Ontario" title="List of protected areas of Ontario">List of parks and protected areas of Ontario</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG/220px-Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG/330px-Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG/440px-Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Algonquin_Cache_Lake_Lookout.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Algonquin_Provincial_Park" title="Algonquin Provincial Park">Algonquin Provincial Park</a>, Cache Lake in the autumn of 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The province consists of three main geographical regions:</p>
<ul>
<li>The thinly populated <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> in the northwestern and central portions, which comprises over half the land area of Ontario. Although this area mostly does not support agriculture, it is rich in <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">minerals</a> and in part covered by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Canadian_Shield_forests" title="Central Canadian Shield forests">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_Canadian_Shield_forests" title="Midwestern Canadian Shield forests">Midwestern Canadian Shield forests</a>, studded with lakes and rivers. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ontario" title="Northern Ontario">Northern Ontario</a> is subdivided into two sub-regions: <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Ontario" title="Northwestern Ontario">Northwestern Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Ontario" title="Northeastern Ontario">Northeastern Ontario</a>.</li>
<li>The virtually unpopulated <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay_Lowlands" title="Hudson Bay Lowlands">Hudson Bay Lowlands</a> in the extreme north and northeast, mainly swampy and sparsely forested.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a> which is further sub-divided into four regions; <a href="/wiki/Central_Ontario" title="Central Ontario">Central Ontario</a> (although not actually the province's geographic centre), <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ontario" title="Eastern Ontario">Eastern Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Ontario" title="Southwestern Ontario">Southwestern Ontario</a> (parts of which were formerly referred to as Western Ontario).</li>
</ul>
<p>Despite the absence of any mountainous terrain in the province, there are large areas of uplands, particularly within the Canadian Shield which traverses the province from northwest to southeast and also above the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Escarpment" title="Niagara Escarpment">Niagara Escarpment</a> which crosses the south. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Ishpatina_Ridge" title="Ishpatina Ridge">Ishpatina Ridge</a> at 693 metres (2,274 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Temagami" title="Temagami">Temagami</a>, Northeastern Ontario. In the south, elevations of over 500 m (1,640 ft) are surpassed near Collingwood, above the Blue Mountains in the Dundalk Highlands and in hilltops near the <a href="/wiki/Madawaska_River_(Ontario)" title="Madawaska River (Ontario)">Madawaska River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Renfrew_County" title="Renfrew County">Renfrew County</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Carolinian_forest" title="Carolinian forest">Carolinian forest</a> zone covers most of the southwestern region of the province. The temperate and fertile Great Lakes-Saint Lawrence Valley in the south is part of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Great_Lakes_lowland_forests" title="Eastern Great Lakes lowland forests">Eastern Great Lakes lowland forests</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> where the forest has now been largely replaced by agriculture, industrial and urban development. A well-known geographic feature is <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">Niagara Falls</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Escarpment" title="Niagara Escarpment">Niagara Escarpment</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Seaway" title="Saint Lawrence Seaway">Saint Lawrence Seaway</a> allows navigation to and from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> as far inland as <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay" title="Thunder Bay">Thunder Bay</a> in Northwestern Ontario. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ontario" title="Northern Ontario">Northern Ontario</a> occupies roughly 87 percent of the surface area of the province; conversely Southern Ontario contains 94 percent of the population.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Point_Pelee_National_Park" title="Point Pelee National Park">Point Pelee</a> is a peninsula of Lake Erie in southwestern Ontario (near <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">Windsor</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan" title="Detroit, Michigan">Detroit, Michigan</a>) that is the southernmost extent of Canada's mainland. <a href="/wiki/Pelee,_Ontario" title="Pelee, Ontario">Pelee Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Island_(Lake_Erie)" title="Middle Island (Lake Erie)">Middle Island</a> in Lake Erie extend slightly farther. All are south of <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42°N</a> – slightly farther south than the northern border of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Ontario#Climate" title="Geography of Ontario">Geography of Ontario § Climate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ON_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1053" data-file-width="900" height="351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/ON_koppen.svg/300px-ON_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/ON_koppen.svg/450px-ON_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/ON_koppen.svg/600px-ON_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ON_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Ontario</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1979" data-file-width="2974" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg/220px-Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg/330px-Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg/440px-Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Ontario_-_Sandbanks_Provincial_Park_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Summer at <a href="/wiki/Sandbanks_Provincial_Park" title="Sandbanks Provincial Park">Sandbanks Provincial Park</a> on Lake Ontario.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of Ontario varies by season and location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC-16">[16]</a></sup> It is affected by three air sources: cold, dry, arctic air from the north (dominant factor during the winter months, and for a longer part of the year in far northern Ontario); Pacific polar air crossing in from the western Canadian Prairies/US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Plains" title="Northern Plains">Northern Plains</a>; and warm, moist air from the Gulf of Mexico and the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCgeo_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-UBCgeo-17">[17]</a></sup> The effects of these major air masses on temperature and precipitation depend mainly on latitude, proximity to major bodies of water and to a small extent, terrain relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCgeo_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-UBCgeo-17">[17]</a></sup> In general, most of Ontario's climate is classified as humid continental.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCgeo_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-UBCgeo-17">[17]</a></sup> Ontario has three main climatic regions.</p>
<p>The surrounding Great Lakes greatly influence the climatic region of southern Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-EC-16">[16]</a></sup> During the fall and winter months, heat stored from the lakes is released, moderating the climate near the shores of the lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPA-18">[18]</a></sup> This gives some parts of southern Ontario milder winters than mid-continental areas at lower latitudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPA_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPA-18">[18]</a></sup> Parts of Southwestern Ontario (generally south of a line from Sarnia-Toronto) have a moderate <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa</i>), similar to that of the inland <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic states</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> portion of the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>. The region has warm to hot, humid summers and cold winters. Annual precipitation ranges from 750–1,000 mm (30–39 in) and is well distributed throughout the year. Most of this region lies in the lee of the Great Lakes, making for abundant snow in some areas. In December 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Snowbelt" title="Snowbelt">snowbelt</a> set a new record when it was hit by more than a metre of snow within 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The next climatic region is Central and Eastern Ontario which has a moderate <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (Köppen <i>Dfb</i>). This region has warm and sometimes hot summers with colder, longer winters, ample snowfall (even in regions not directly in the snowbelts) and annual precipitation similar to the rest of Southern Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCgeo_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-UBCgeo-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG/220px-Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG/330px-Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG/440px-Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Escarpment_at_Bruce_Peninsula.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Escarpment" title="Niagara Escarpment">Niagara Escarpment</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Peninsula" title="Bruce Peninsula">Bruce Peninsula</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the northeastern parts of Ontario, extending far as south as <a href="/wiki/Kirkland_Lake" title="Kirkland Lake">Kirkland Lake</a>, the cold waters of Hudson Bay depress summer temperatures, making it cooler than other locations at similar latitudes. The same is true on the northern shore of Lake Superior, which cools hot humid air from the south, leading to cooler summer temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBCgeo_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-UBCgeo-17">[17]</a></sup> Along the eastern shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">Lake Superior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Huron" title="Lake Huron">Lake Huron</a> winter temperatures are slightly moderated but come with frequent heavy <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">lake-effect snow</a> squalls that increase seasonal snowfall totals upwards of 3 m (10 ft) in some places. These regions have higher annual precipitation in some case over 100 cm (39 in). The northernmost parts of Ontario – primarily north of 50°N – have a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a> (Köppen <i>Dfc</i>) with long, severely cold winters and short, cool to warm summers with dramatic temperature changes possible in all seasons. With no major mountain ranges blocking sinking <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a>, temperatures of −40 °C (−40 °F) are not uncommon; snowfall remains on the ground for sometimes over half the year. Snowfall accumulation can be high in some areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-EC-16">[16]</a></sup> Precipitation is generally less than 70 cm (28 in) and peaks in the summer months in the form of showers or thunderstorms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-EC-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Severe <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorms</a> peak in summer. <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London</a>, situated in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern</a> <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Ontario" title="Southwestern Ontario">(Southwestern)</a> Ontario, has the most lightning strikes per year in Canada, averaging 34 days of thunderstorm activity per year. In a typical year, Ontario averages 11 confirmed <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> touchdowns. However, over the last 4 years,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> it has had upwards of 20 tornado touchdowns per year, with the highest frequency occurring in the Windsor-Essex – Chatham Kent area, though few are very destructive (the majority between F0 to F2 on the <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">Fujita scale</a>). Ontario had a record 29 tornadoes in both 2006 and 2009. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">Tropical depression</a> remnants occasionally bring heavy rains and winds in the south, but are rarely deadly. A notable exception was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hurricane Hazel</a> which struck Southern Ontario centred on Toronto, in October 1954.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ontario" title="History of Ontario">History of Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_evolution">Territorial evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Territorial evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif"><img alt="When Canada was formed in 1867 its provinces were a relatively narrow strip in the southeast, with vast territories in the interior. It grew by adding British Columbia in 1871, P.E.I. in 1873, the British Arctic Islands in 1880, and Newfoundland in 1949; meanwhile, its provinces grew both in size and number at the expense of its territories." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="864" data-file-width="1000" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/220px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/330px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif/440px-Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Evolution of the borders of Ontario.<br/>
View <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Canada_provinces_evolution_2.gif" title="Canada provinces evolution 2.gif">full resolution</a> for time-lapsed evolution</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Land was not legally subdivided into administrative units until a treaty had been concluded with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Proclamation_of_1763" title="Royal Proclamation of 1763">Aboriginal people ceding the land</a>. In 1788, while part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Quebec_(1763%E2%80%9391)" title="Province of Quebec (1763–91)">Province of Quebec</a>, southern Ontario was divided into four <a href="/wiki/District#Ontario" title="District">districts</a>: <a href="/wiki/Western_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Western District, Upper Canada">Hesse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Eastern District, Upper Canada">Lunenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midland_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Midland District, Upper Canada">Mecklenburg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Home_District" title="Home District">Nassau</a>.</p>
<p>In 1792, the four districts were renamed: Hesse became the Western District, Lunenburg became the Eastern District, Mecklenburg became the Midland District, and Nassau became the Home District. Counties were created within the districts.</p>
<p>By 1798, there were eight districts: Eastern, Home, <a href="/wiki/Johnstown_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Johnstown District, Upper Canada">Johnstown</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_District,_Upper_Canada" title="London District, Upper Canada">London</a>, Midland, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_District" title="Newcastle District">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niagara_District" title="Niagara District">Niagara</a>, and Western.</p>
<p>By 1826, there were eleven districts: <a href="/wiki/Bathurst_District" title="Bathurst District">Bathurst</a>, Eastern, <a href="/wiki/Gore_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Gore District, Upper Canada">Gore</a>, Home, Johnstown, London, Midland, Newcastle, Niagara, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_District" title="Ottawa District">Ottawa</a>, and Western.</p>
<p>By 1838, there were twenty districts: Bathurst, Brock, Colbourne, <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_District" title="Dalhousie District">Dalhousie</a>, Eastern, Gore, Home, Huron, Johnstown, London, Midland, Newcastle, Niagara, Ottawa, Prince Edward, <a href="/wiki/Simcoe_County" title="Simcoe County">Simcoe</a>, Talbot, Victoria, <a href="/wiki/Wellington_District,_Upper_Canada" title="Wellington District, Upper Canada">Wellington</a>, and Western.</p>
<p>In 1849, the districts of southern Ontario were abolished by the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">county</a> governments took over certain municipal responsibilities. The Province of Canada also began creating <i>districts</i> in sparsely populated Northern Ontario with the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Algoma_District" title="Algoma District">Algoma District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nipissing_District" title="Nipissing District">Nipissing District</a> in 1858.</p>
<p>The borders of Ontario, its new name in 1867, were provisionally expanded north and west. When the Province of Canada was formed, its borders were not entirely clear, and Ontario claimed eventually to reach all the way to the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>. With Canada's acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert's Land">Rupert's Land</a>, Ontario was interested in clearly defining its borders, especially since some of the new areas in which it was interested were rapidly growing. After the federal government asked Ontario to pay for construction in the new disputed area, the province asked for an elaboration on its limits, and its boundary was moved north to the <a href="/wiki/51st_parallel_north" title="51st parallel north">51st parallel north</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern and western boundaries of Ontario were in dispute after <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>. Ontario's right to Northwestern Ontario was determined by the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> in 1884 and confirmed by the <i>Canada (Ontario Boundary) Act, 1889</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>. By 1899, there were seven northern districts: Algoma, Manitoulin, Muskoka, Nipissing, Parry Sound, Rainy River, and Thunder Bay. Four more northern districts were created between 1907 and 1912: Cochrane, Kenora, Sudbury and Timiskaming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact">European contact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: European contact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/220px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/330px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG/440px-UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UnitedEmpireLoyalistsHamilton.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of <a href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalist" title="United Empire Loyalist">United Empire Loyalists</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a> on <a href="/wiki/Main_Street_(Hamilton,_Ontario)" title="Main Street (Hamilton, Ontario)">Main Street East</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to the arrival of the Europeans, the region was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">Algonquian</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ojibwa_people" title="Ojibwa people">Ojibwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">Cree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algonquin_people" title="Algonquin people">Algonquin</a>) in the northern/western portions, and <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a> and Wyandot (Huron) tribes more in the south/east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> During the 17th century, the Algonquians and Hurons fought the <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Wars" title="Beaver Wars">Beaver Wars</a> against the Iroquois.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The French explorer <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Br%C3%BBl%C3%A9" title="Étienne Brûlé">Étienne Brûlé</a> explored part of the area in 1610–12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The English explorer <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> sailed into <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a> in 1611 and claimed the area for <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Samuel_de_Champlain" title="Samuel de Champlain">Samuel de Champlain</a> reached Lake Huron in 1615, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> missionaries began to establish posts along the Great Lakes. French settlement was hampered by their hostilities with the Iroquois, who allied themselves with the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefrenchshouldvewon_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefrenchshouldvewon-35">[35]</a></sup> From 1634 to 1640, Hurons were devastated by European infectious diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, to which they had no immunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> By 1700, the Iroquois had seceded from Ontario and the Mississaugas of the Ojibwa had settled the north shore of Lake Ontario.</p>
<p>The British established <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> on Hudson Bay in the late 17th century and began a struggle for domination of Ontario. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">1763 Treaty of Paris</a> ended the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> by awarding nearly all of <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">France's North American possessions</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>) to Britain. The region was annexed to Quebec in 1774.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The first European settlements were in 1782–1784 when 5,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalists" title="United Empire Loyalists">American loyalists</a> entered what is now Ontario following the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> granted them 200 acres (81 ha) land and other items with which to rebuild their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefrenchshouldvewon_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-thefrenchshouldvewon-35">[35]</a></sup> The British also set up reservations in Ontario for the <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_people" title="Mohawk people">Mohawks</a> who had fought for the British and had lost their land in New York state. Other Iroquois were resettled in 1784 at the <a href="/wiki/Six_Nations_of_the_Grand_River" title="Six Nations of the Grand River">Six Nations</a> reserve at the west end of Lake Ontario.</p>
<p>The population of Canada west of the St. Lawrence-Ottawa River confluence substantially increased during this period, a fact recognized by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Act_of_1791" title="Constitutional Act of 1791">Constitutional Act of 1791</a>, which split Quebec into <a href="/wiki/The_Canadas" title="The Canadas">the Canadas</a>: <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> southwest of the St. Lawrence-Ottawa River confluence, and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a> east of it. <a href="/wiki/John_Graves_Simcoe" title="John Graves Simcoe">John Graves Simcoe</a> was appointed Upper Canada's first <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(Canada)" title="Lieutenant governor (Canada)">Lieutenant governor</a> in 1793.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Canada">Upper Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Upper Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a></div>
<p>American troops in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> invaded Upper Canada across the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">Niagara River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_River" title="Detroit River">Detroit River</a>, but were defeated and pushed back by the British, Canadian <a href="/wiki/Fencibles" title="Fencibles">fencibles</a> and militias, and <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> warriors. However, eventually the Americans gained control of Lake Erie and Lake Ontario. During the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_York" title="Battle of York">Battle of York</a> in 1813, American troops occupied the <a href="/wiki/York,_Upper_Canada" title="York, Upper Canada">Town of York</a>. The Americans looted the town and burned the Parliament Buildings during the brief occupation.</p>
<p>After the War of 1812, relative stability allowed for increasing numbers of immigrants to arrive from Europe rather than from the United States. As was the case in the previous decades, this immigration shift was encouraged by the colonial leaders. Despite affordable and often free land, many arriving newcomers, mostly from Britain and Ireland, found frontier life with the harsh climate difficult, and some of those with the means eventually returned home or went south. However, population growth far exceeded emigration in the decades that followed. It was a mostly agrarian-based society, but canal projects and a new network of plank roads spurred greater trade within the colony and with the United States, thereby improving previously damaged relations over time.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ontario_1718.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="1201" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ontario_1718.jpg/220px-Ontario_1718.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ontario_1718.jpg/330px-Ontario_1718.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ontario_1718.jpg/440px-Ontario_1718.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ontario_1718.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lower Ontario in 1718, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guillaume_de_L%27Isle" title="Guillaume de L'Isle">Guillaume de L'Isle</a> map, approximate province area highlighted.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Meanwhile, Ontario's numerous waterways aided travel and transportation into the interior and supplied <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">water power</a> for development. As the population increased, so did the industries and transportation networks, which in turn led to further development. By the end of the century, Ontario vied with Quebec as the nation's leader in terms of growth in population, industry, arts and communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unrest in the colony began to chafe against the aristocratic <a href="/wiki/Family_Compact" title="Family Compact">Family Compact</a> who governed while benefiting economically from the region's resources, and who did not allow elected bodies power. This resentment spurred republican ideals and sowed the seeds for early <a href="/wiki/Canadian_nationalism" title="Canadian nationalism">Canadian nationalism</a>. Accordingly, rebellion in favour of <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a> rose in both regions; <a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_Papineau" title="Louis-Joseph Papineau">Louis-Joseph Papineau</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada_Rebellion" title="Lower Canada Rebellion">Lower Canada Rebellion</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie" title="William Lyon Mackenzie">William Lyon Mackenzie</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada_Rebellion" title="Upper Canada Rebellion">Upper Canada Rebellion</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada_West">Canada West</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Canada West">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a></div>
<p>Although both rebellions were put down in short order, the British government sent <a href="/wiki/John_Lambton,_1st_Earl_of_Durham" title="John Lambton, 1st Earl of Durham">Lord Durham</a> to investigate the causes of the unrest. He recommended that self-government be granted and that Lower and Upper Canada be re-joined in an attempt to assimilate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French Canadians</a>. Accordingly, the two colonies were merged into the Province of Canada by the <i><a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1840" title="Act of Union 1840">Act of Union 1840</a></i>, with the capital at <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston</a>, and Upper Canada becoming known as <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Canada West</a>. Parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-government</a> was granted in 1848. There were heavy waves of immigration in the 1840s, and the population of Canada West more than doubled by 1851 over the previous decade. As a result, for the first time the English-speaking population of Canada West surpassed the French-speaking population of <a href="/wiki/Canada_East" title="Canada East">Canada East</a>, tilting the representative balance of power.</p>
<p>An economic boom in the 1850s coincided with railway expansion across the province, further increasing the economic strength of Central Canada. With the repeal of the <a href="/wiki/Corn_Laws" title="Corn Laws">Corn Laws</a> and a reciprocity agreement in place with United States, various industries such as timber, mining, farming and alcohol distilling benefited tremendously.</p>
<p>A political stalemate between the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">French</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">English</a>-speaking legislators, as well as fear of aggression from the United States during and immediately after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, led the political elite to hold a series of conferences in the 1860s to effect a broader federal union of all <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North American</a> colonies. The <i>British North America Act</i> took effect on July 1, 1867, establishing the Dominion of Canada, initially with four provinces: Nova Scotia, New Brunswick, Quebec and Ontario. The Province of Canada was divided into Ontario and Quebec so that each linguistic group would have its own province. Both Quebec and Ontario were required by section 93 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act,_1867" title="Constitution Act, 1867">British North America Act</a> to safeguard existing educational rights and privileges of Protestant and the Catholic minority. Thus, separate Catholic schools and <a href="/wiki/Board_of_education" title="Board of education">school boards</a> were permitted in Ontario. However, neither province had a constitutional requirement to protect its French- or English-speaking minority. Toronto was formally established as Ontario's provincial capital.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provincehood">Provincehood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Provincehood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One_London_Place_Night.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/One_London_Place_Night.JPG/220px-One_London_Place_Night.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/One_London_Place_Night.JPG/330px-One_London_Place_Night.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/One_London_Place_Night.JPG/440px-One_London_Place_Night.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Downtown <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London</a> at night.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="624" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg/220px-VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg/330px-VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg/440px-VEDaySparksStreet1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg/220px-Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg/330px-Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg/440px-Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skyline_of_Toronto_viewed_from_Harbour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, the capital of Ontario</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Once constituted as a province, Ontario proceeded to assert its economic and legislative power. In 1872, the lawyer <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Mowat" title="Oliver Mowat">Oliver Mowat</a> became <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">Premier of Ontario</a> and remained as premier until 1896. He fought for provincial rights, weakening the power of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">federal government</a> in provincial matters, usually through well-argued appeals to the Judicial Committee of the Privy Council. His battles with the federal government greatly <a href="/wiki/Decentralization" title="Decentralization">decentralized</a> Canada, giving the provinces far more power than <a href="/wiki/John_A._Macdonald" title="John A. Macdonald">John A. Macdonald</a> had intended. He consolidated and expanded Ontario's educational and provincial institutions, created districts in Northern Ontario, and fought to ensure that those parts of Northwestern Ontario not historically part of Upper Canada (the vast areas north and west of the Lake Superior-Hudson Bay watershed, known as the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Keewatin" title="District of Keewatin">District of Keewatin</a>) would become part of Ontario, a victory embodied in the <i>Canada (Ontario Boundary) Act, 1889</i>. He also presided over the emergence of the province into the economic powerhouse of Canada. Mowat was the creator of what is often called <i>Empire Ontario</i>.</p>
<p>Beginning with Sir John A. Macdonald's <a href="/wiki/National_Policy" title="National Policy">National Policy</a> (1879) and the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">Canadian Pacific Railway</a> (1875–1885) through Northern Ontario and the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Prairies" title="Canadian Prairies">Canadian Prairies</a> to <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, Ontario manufacturing and industry flourished. However, population increase slowed after a large recession hit the province in 1893, thus slowing growth drastically but for only a few years. Many newly arrived immigrants and others moved west along the railway to the Prairie Provinces and British Columbia, sparsely settling Northern Ontario.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">Mineral</a> exploitation accelerated in the late 19th century, leading to the rise of important mining centres in the northeast, such as <a href="/wiki/Greater_Sudbury" title="Greater Sudbury">Sudbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt,_Ontario" title="Cobalt, Ontario">Cobalt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timmins" title="Timmins">Timmins</a>. The province harnessed its water power to generate hydro-electric power and created the state-controlled Hydro-Electric Power Commission of Ontario, later <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Hydro" title="Ontario Hydro">Ontario Hydro</a>. The availability of cheap electric power further facilitated the development of industry. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Canada" title="Ford Motor Company of Canada">Ford Motor Company of Canada</a> was established in 1904. <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Canada" title="General Motors Canada">General Motors Canada</a> was formed in 1918. The motor vehicle industry became the most lucrative industry for the Ontario economy during the 20th century.</p>
<p>In July 1912, the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Ontario" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Ontario">Conservative</a> government of Sir <a href="/wiki/James_Whitney" title="James Whitney">James Whitney</a> issued <a href="/wiki/Regulation_17" title="Regulation 17">Regulation 17</a> which severely limited the availability of French-language schooling to the province's French-speaking minority. French Canadians reacted with outrage, journalist <a href="/wiki/Henri_Bourassa" title="Henri Bourassa">Henri Bourassa</a> denouncing the "Prussians of Ontario". The regulation was eventually repealed in 1927.</p>
<p>Influenced by events in the United States, the government of Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Hearst" title="William Howard Hearst">William Hearst</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_Canada" title="Prohibition in Canada">prohibition</a> of alcoholic drinks in 1916 with the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Temperance_Act" title="Ontario Temperance Act">Ontario Temperance Act</a>. However, residents could distill and retain their own personal supply, and liquor producers could continue distillation and export for sale, allowing this already sizeable industry to strengthen further. Ontario became a hotbed for the illegal smuggling of liquor and the biggest supplier into the United States, which was under complete <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">prohibition</a>. Prohibition in Ontario came to an end in 1927 with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Liquor_Control_Board_of_Ontario" title="Liquor Control Board of Ontario">Liquor Control Board of Ontario</a> under the government of <a href="/wiki/Howard_Ferguson" title="Howard Ferguson">Howard Ferguson</a>. The sale and consumption of liquor, wine, and beer are still controlled by some of the most extreme laws in North America to ensure that strict community standards and revenue generation from the alcohol retail monopoly are upheld. In April 2007, Ontario Member of Provincial Parliament <a href="/wiki/Kim_Craitor" title="Kim Craitor">Kim Craitor</a> suggested that local brewers should be able to sell their beer in local corner stores; however, the motion was quickly rejected by Premier <a href="/wiki/Dalton_McGuinty" title="Dalton McGuinty">Dalton McGuinty</a>.</p>
<p>The post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> period was one of exceptional prosperity and growth. Ontario has been the recipients of most immigration to Canada, largely immigrants from war-torn Europe in the 1950s and 1960s and following changes in federal <a href="/wiki/Immigration_law" title="Immigration law">immigration law</a>, a massive influx of non-Europeans since the 1970s. From a largely <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnically</a> British province, Ontario has rapidly become culturally very diverse.</p>
<p>The nationalist movement in Quebec, particularly after the election of the <i><a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">Parti Québécois</a></i> in 1976, contributed to driving many businesses and English-speaking people out of Quebec to Ontario, and as a result Toronto surpassed <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> as the largest city and economic centre of Canada.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="it's not clear that many businesses were driven away to Ontario, and it's not clear that this led to Toronto becoming the largest city. Other factors were arguably more important. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Depressed economic conditions in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Maritime Provinces</a> have also resulted in de-population of those provinces in the 20th century, with heavy migration into Ontario.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="what is considered here heavy migration. do we have numbers? (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Ontario's official language is <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboot_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-aboot-5">[5]</a></sup> Numerous <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a> services are available under the <a href="/wiki/French_Language_Services_Act" title="French Language Services Act">French Language Services Act</a> of 1990 in designated areas where sizeable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">francophone</a> populations exist.</p>

<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">12,851,821</td>
<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.7%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/Canada_2016_Census" title="Canada 2016 Census">2016</a></th>
<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">13,448,494</td>
<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.6%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Canada" title="Statistics Canada">Statistics Canada</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Canada_2011_Census" title="Canada 2011 Census">2011 census</a>, Ontario had a population of 12,851,821 living in 4,887,508 of its 5,308,785 total dwellings, a 5.7 percent change from its 2006 population of 12,160,282. With a land area of 908,607.67 km<sup>2</sup> (350,815.38 sq mi), it had a population density of 14.1/km<sup>2</sup> (36.6/sq mi) in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StatCan2011_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-StatCan2011-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2013, Statistics Canada estimated the province's population to be 13,537,994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estimates_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-estimates-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The percentages given below add to more than 100 percent because of dual responses (e.g., "French and Canadian" response generates an entry both in the category "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French Canadian</a>" and in the category "<a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a>").</p>
<p>The majority of Ontarians are of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_Canadian" title="English Canadian">English</a> or other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Canadian" title="European Canadian">European descent</a> including large Scottish, Irish and Italian communities. Slightly less than 5 percent of the population of Ontario is <a href="/wiki/Franco-Ontarian" title="Franco-Ontarian">Franco-Ontarian</a>, that is those whose native tongue is French, although those with French ancestry account for 11 percent of the population. In relation to natural increase or inter-provincial migration, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">immigration</a> is a huge population growth force in Ontario, as it has been over the last two centuries. More recent sources of <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrants</a> with large or growing communities in Ontario include <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (July 2017)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin Americans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africans</a>. Most populations have settled in the larger urban centres.</p>
<p>In 2011, 25.9 percent of the population consisted of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visible_minorities" title="Visible minorities">visible minorities</a> and 2.4 percent of the population was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_in_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples in Canada">Aboriginal</a>, mostly of <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people_(Canada)" title="Métis people (Canada)">Métis</a> descent. There was also a small number of <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> people in the province. The number of Aboriginal people and visible minorities has been increasing at a faster rate than the general population of Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, the largest religious denominations in Ontario were the Roman Catholic Church (with 31.4% of the population), the United Church of Canada (7.5%), and the Anglican Church (6.1%). 23.1% of Ontarians had no religious affiliation, making it the second-largest religious grouping in the province after Roman Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census-religion_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-religion-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
